Free Discussion

Sayings of the 93-Year-Old Ma Xiangbo

Forgetting What One Has Read Is the Most Painful Thing in Life 146

— Lai Bei

Reading foreign books involves nothing more than reasoning and narration. In fact, speeches also involve reasoning and narration. The so-called "Belle Oration" also aims to convey meanings clearly, express rich emotions and profound thoughts, move people, and persuade them to do good. Actors in plays only make people relieve boredom and laugh. The popular speeches nowadays also only aim to win applause and cheers from the audience, which is not that different from acting. They do not prompt people to think deeply, nor do they inspire people to sing or weep, which is a great loss to the meaning of speeches.

The best Chinese book for narration is Sima Qian's "Records of the Grand Historian." My teacher, Chao Deli, once said, "Even foreign countries cannot match the writing style of Sima Qian. The writing style of the 'Records of the Grand Historian' is concise, clear, and transparent. He uses just a few words to describe historical facts, which can be regarded as the essence of narration."

Reading Chinese books focuses on recitation, so many people can cite classical allusions from memory. In the past, there was a Sun Dengshan, a Hanlin official from Zhejiang, who was a favorite disciple of Zhang Xiangtao (Zi Dong). His memory was truly good, and he could recite the Thirteen Classics from beginning to end, which was truly not easy, and I admire him greatly for this. Strangely, after reading many books, one sometimes forgets everything completely, and sometimes only some shadows remain. In fact, foreign languages and Chinese languages seem to be two different things. Sometimes, after reading many foreign books, when one wants to pick up a pen and write some Chinese characters, one cannot even recall the sentences. I suffer greatly. When outsiders come to ask me to write inscriptions or compose poems, I have to rack my brains and strain my blood, because my brain is as empty as a drawer. I have to pull them out one by one and search for traces in the books that I have forgotten completely. (Han's note: Old Master Xiang is modest and magnanimous. In fact, his memory is very strong, and he can often point out the mysteries and contradictions in the words of the ancients.)

In my opinion, forgetting what one has read is the most painful thing in life.

Yesterday's title, "Settled in a Careless Manner" (活囫圇了結), was a mistake for "Swallowing the Date Whole" (囫圇呑了結). This is a correction.

A Record of Taking Over the Dead Market of Jiangwan 147

— Ms. Hua

On the morning of May 19th at 8:00 AM, government personnel and news reporters gathered at the Joint Association, ready to depart and take over Jiangwan, west of Songhu Road. The passes stated that only 18 people were allowed. The reporters found no room to squeeze in and looked at each other in dismay. Jin Xiongbai arrived the latest and was caught off guard, looking the most anxious. Xu Xinyi arrived the earliest and had already made contact, appearing the most calm. The rest were discussing animatedly, some suggesting retreat and others suggesting a charge. No one could reach a consensus. In the end, they all went together, with Ma Chonggan's car leading the way. Each car had to follow closely so as not to get lost and overcome the difficulties of being questioned along the way. Unexpectedly, my car was particularly slow, and the driver was not skilled. As a result, we fell behind. Jiang Hongjiao and Zhang Youde were afraid of getting lost and not receiving news, so they were extremely anxious and urged the driver to step on the gas. However, the driver was covered in sweat and nothing helped. Near the New World, a red light flashed, and the car in front sped past, losing sight of us. Thus, we could not see those who had gone before nor those who would come after, and the car wandered alone. Everyone was scratching their heads anxiously, blaming Zhang San and complaining about Li Si. Fortunately, Mr. Ma's car was waiting at Hongkou Park, and everyone finally felt relieved.

Jiangwan covers an area of ninety square li and four fen, with six thousand one hundred and four households and more than seven thousand one hundred houses. Now, nineteen out of ten are destroyed. The number of households with family losses that have been registered has reached two thousand six hundred and fourteen. The main street with department stores has become a scorched earth. No houses survived. Jiangwan, which was previously regarded as a scenic area with a rich Western European Swiss flavor, is now like a dead city in Belgium after the war, with no trace of human habitation. Japanese soldiers were constantly marching along the way, often showing murderous faces. The Labor University was riddled with bullet holes. In front of the broken wall was a Japanese gun rack with guns and bullets. Mr. Zhou stood beside it, and the reporters competed to take pictures. Who knew that two Japanese officers would suddenly get out of the car, brandishing their power. A large number of cameras were almost in danger. Mr. Li, a reporter for the Continental Daily, was quick-witted and captured a shot. This photo is worth more than usual.

At 11:30 AM, representatives from both sides and neutral countries held a handover ceremony at the Cultural College Japanese Headquarters and signed the handover document. The Japanese representative, Akazawa, shook hands with our side's Dai, Liang, and Li committee members and drank champagne to say goodbye. Alas, since Chinese territory has not been transferred, how can there be a takeover? Nothing in the world is more ridiculous. At 12:00 PM, Dr. Fei Kunian and I hired a car to go north of the town, intending to delve into the interior and pay tribute to the traces of war. Along the way, the birds were crying and the flowers were falling, and the water was green and the wind was clear, which made one feel "the country still stands, but in the spring, the city is overgrown." I saw the Keyi Village Municipal School. The janitor said that the school had been occupied by the Japanese army. On the 18th, before leaving, they took away a sandbox designed to resist Japan. It was expected that its return would provoke the Chinese people. The classics were gone, and the tables, chairs, and organs had disappeared. The fences were completely removed, and the glass windows were completely shattered. The lush grass in the playground was like the hair of prisoners, overgrown and messy, making it impossible to step on. Reflecting on the past and thinking about the present, I couldn't help but shed tears. I went west again to Xitang Village, but I saw that all the houses had been almost completely destroyed by Japanese planes. What met the eye was nothing but ruins and rubble. The villagers, carrying their young and leading their women, were building thatched huts, like swallows carrying mud in spring, working hard in every way. Their faces all reflected the tragedy in their hearts. They did not know where the tears would come from. The Municipal Tao Bay Elementary School was also buried among them. The painstaking creation was hit with disaster in a single day. The cruelty of destroying culture was worse than the burning of books by Qin Shi Huang. This is truly a fatal wound to our nation.

Tidbits 148

— Ping

Dai Jitao, the president of the Examination Yuan of the National Government, was beaten and insulted by students while giving a speech in the wartime capital of Xi'an… The newspapers have been reporting this incident for the past few days. These young people dare to despise party discipline and insult the "elders of the party," which is tantamount to destroying the "dignity and sanctity of the party." In fact, whether the party is worthy of "dignity and sanctity" is another question, but let's talk about the "elders of the party."

There is always a so-called "elder faction" in any country's political party. Our country's Kuomintang is no exception, and there is more than one elder. I remember that in recent years, every time a party struggle led to a civil war, the elders would run around to all sides, trying to mediate and reconcile, exhausting their ability to quell the unrest. However, the result was still inevitably a "war." Due to the worsening situation, it was difficult for them to be elders! Since the outbreak of the September 18th National Crisis until now, the government has been sitting idly by, allowing the country to be ceded and rights lost. In the absence of any way to deal with the situation, the "elders of the party" have been enduring the pain and enjoying themselves, and not a single one has been willing to speak out righteously and resolve the national crisis! Apart from the patriotic people who do not forget their "ownership" status and cry out in pain, almost no one is advising the government. Hey! "Elders of the party," both internally and externally, are like this, so what else is there to say? Therefore, Dai's humiliation was a normal reaction. What is so rare about it?

A Misunderstanding About Qiyakou 149

— Yanzi

Liuhe, Yanglinkou, and Qiyakou are all important fortresses along the Yangtze River. During the Wanli period of the Ming Dynasty, when Japanese pirates invaded, Fengxian and Nanhui along the coast (at that time, Fengxian was under the jurisdiction of Lou County and Nanhui was under the jurisdiction of Shanghai, and the counties had not yet been separated) and Taicang and Changshu along the river were all areas ravaged by Japanese pirates. The court ordered Qi Jiguang to lead his troops to suppress the pirates and stationed a large army at Huijiao. Beacon towers were set up along the line, reaching all the way to Hangzhou, totaling one hundred and fifty-three towers. The three towers in Nanhui still exist at the old site. Whenever a Japanese warship docked, a fire would be lit as a signal to communicate military intelligence. In the Huangdu area of Taicang, Japanese pirates entered by surprise and carried out a very tragic massacre (according to research, the only people who can be called true Huangdu people today are the Zhang, Jin, Wang, and Wan families). The villagers fled to the four townships of Zhangyan and Qinglong Temple. The Japanese pirates followed and arrived. The Weituo deity enshrined in Qinglong Temple manifested himself in the clouds and scared away the Japanese pirates. At that time, Qi Jiguang heard the alarm and led his entire fleet into the river mouth, surrounding and suppressing the pirates on all sides. All the Japanese pirates were wiped out. People praised his merits and named the place "Lord Qi's Mouth." Over time, it was distorted and mistakenly called Qiyakou, which is a great loss to the ancient people's intention of commemorating and admiring the meritorious deeds. This is recorded for those who are familiar with geography to consult.

Editor's note: During this Japanese invasion, the people of Huangdu all fled to Zhangyan and were fortunate enough to be spared. Therefore, the incense offering at Qinglong Temple on March 15th was extremely grand, which was also due to this reason.

Anecdotes from the Old Capital

Camel Bells 150

— Zhu An

In the past, the capital officials would jocularly compare camels to Hanlin officials, saying that they were similar in their high view and slow pace. They also said that their entangled networks could obstruct passersby, similar to the Hanlin officials forming factions and providing assistance. This saying probably already existed in the Ming Dynasty. The camel is a thing that, during the harsh winter weather, has the ability to shoulder heavy responsibilities and go far. Its huge body and thick, soft fur give it a kind and approachable air. It is truly a sacred animal of the north. All those who transport coal must use this animal. From the Western Hills to the city, one often encounters them day and night in the autumn and winter seasons. About ten camels form a team, their noses pierced with rope and connected continuously. The last camel has a large bell hanging from its neck, so the person leading the way can know that the camel is safe by listening to the sound of the bell, without having to care for it. The sound is deep, turbid, and slow, and whenever the frost is clear and the wind is tight, it is like a call and response, which makes people feel as if they are hearing an ancient song of leaving the border. If one encounters camel bells and then hears the sound of a car horn, then the new and the old, the fast and the slow, show the difference in the era and the great distance. In my opinion, the camel bell can represent the national character of the north, and the camel team and the car traveling side by side on the road are enough to represent the mixed composition of the new and old cultures of the northern capital, traveling side by side without conflicting. By April and May, the camel's hair falls off, revealing its skin, and it becomes emaciated and bony, making it look particularly miserable. They are gradually rarely seen in the market, and when it gets hotter, they cannot go out. Once the autumn wind blows a little harder, new hair grows, and they quickly regain a warm and revitalized appearance. Therefore, this thing cannot only not cross the river, but it cannot even be transported between Zhao and Wei. Its nature is unique. They usually carry coal in sacks, and the hands, feet, and faces of the people leading the camels are all stained with coal, which is called coal black.

Opium to Save the Nation? 151

— Meng Zhao

Since the September 18th Incident in the East Province and the January 28th Incident in Shanghai, the enemy's artillery fire has continuously attacked our country, and everyone has been shouting about saving the nation… creating a smoky atmosphere! The ways to save the nation are different. Some are playing dancing to save the nation? Some are playing mahjong to save the nation? Playing games to save the nation? Now, they are going a step further and simply using opium to save the nation; according to reports: "The Chinese National Anti-Drug Association is using all its efforts to protest against the fact that all provinces in the north and south have already implemented the public sale of opium. It is now heard that the central government is carrying out the public sale plan for the provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang. Wu Liande has repeatedly traveled to Beijing and Shanghai to work for this matter."

Late at night, the lights are dim, puffing smoke, lying on a couch, this shackle of the smoke screen, is this saving the nation? Is this destroying the race? Alas! Hateful! Alas! Painful!

Impromptu Poem Presented to My Old Friend Gao Youtang on His Appointment as Censor, Feeling That He Has the Air of a Righteous Official 152

— Tao Zaidong

May you be safe, Censor Gao,

As we meet, our hairs turning white.

The capital teems with officials,

Fire towers watch over mountains and rivers.

Your brow shows urgent concern for the times,

Your writings serve the nation greatly.

The rising sun brings a singing phoenix,

I long for your words all night long.

Minor Tune of "Small Chongshan" 153

— Xie Yucen

Slightly angry, the silver lamp smiles and turns away,

The door is cold in autumn and spring.

A dream urges me on.

The swallows, just flying, are afraid to return.

On the branch, words of farewell,

Sadness will not come again.

The sea air, the old towers,

The songs of fish and dragons are boiling,

Telling of flowers blooming.

For no reason, the zither stirs deep sorrow.

In the human world,

The clear and shallow change to Penglai.

Records of Military Life in Shuang Lou (60) 154

— Master of the Hall of Seeking Happiness

Chapter 8: Boundless Sorrow and Resentment in Confession, Difficult to Expect Open-mindedness; Utmost Song and Dance, Revelry Reveal Authority and Dignity

It is said that Liang Xiaoyun returned home and saw Wei Zhuomou already sitting in the study with An Yutian. He said that Li Wenxia had a reply letter and entrusted Wei Zhuomou to bring it. He was anxious to get the letter to read. Wei Zhuomou casually picked up a page of stationery from the coffee table, unfolded it, and said, "What's written on it is very simple. Yutian has already read it just now. I might as well recite it to you once. There are many unfinished words below. Li Wenxia asked me to convey them orally on her behalf." There were only a few lines scribbled on the letter, only a hundred or so words, very much like a casual note. It said, "I have read your letter. The previous agreement suddenly changed. At first, I was inevitably surprised. Then I thought that you were forced by the situation and could eventually be understood. Since I am of no benefit to you, I should not stand in the way and delay your future. Now I have nothing else to say but to retreat. The previous agreement is naturally cancelled, without any objection. A check is returned herewith. The remaining sentiments are entrusted to Mr. Wei to convey in person. I wish Mr. Yutian and Ms. Xiaoyun a happy marriage." Judging from these few words on the surface alone, this Ms. Li can indeed be said to be the most capable of being open-minded. But it's not that I, Lao Wei, am boasting. In reality, it was still thanks to my eloquence that I persuaded her. At first, when she went to the apartment and received the letter Yutian wrote to her from the tea boy, she was simply filled with anger. Several times she wanted to come to your door and question Yutian alone. Even when I first went to see her, she was crying and making a fuss at me, talking about legal solutions and newspaper questioning. After I used my three-inch tongue to explain to her in detail, I said that the established situation in the world could not be changed, and the ever-changing love in mankind could not be forced. Yutian's new union is related to Yutian's current personal interests. If you truly love Yutian, you should understand Yutian's difficulties. If you simply act on impulse, you will only hurt your feelings, and in the end, you will not be able to reunite. Or even if you can reunite, it will still be of no benefit to each other. You cannot solve the current difficulties, and it is also difficult to maintain it for a long time. Then why bother doing it? Fortunately, she is indeed extremely intelligent. After thinking about my famous words that contained great philosophy, she suddenly woke up and voluntarily tried her best to be a great benevolent and brave sacrifice in the field of love. But she also asked me to say a few words on her behalf. No matter how Yutian treats her, she still loves Yutian very much. In addition to sincerely praying for your happiness in everything, she is determined to go her own way and vows to use her single life to commemorate her past dreamlike love with Yutian. And in order to maintain her independent personality, she will strive on her own from now on. She does not want to rely on anyone. Therefore, she has to return your check in order to avoid the suspicion of using money to buy love. After she has made some achievements in the future, she can also勉徇 Xiaoyun's kindness and maintain a considerable friendship with each other. But it's not possible to talk about this for a while. Please forgive you two."

Last Week's Gold Price First Fell and Then Rebounded 155

Once Passed the 700 Taels Mark on Tuesday

The Fluctuations Were Extremely Dramatic Throughout the Week The changes in the gold price last week were even more dramatic, with a difference of more than ten taels per day. Industry players were at a loss, and major households' inflows and outflows took different paths. At the beginning of the week, the assassination of the Japanese Prime Minister caused a sudden drop, once breaking the 700 taels mark, suddenly reaching 687 taels and 5 mace. Subsequently, overseas silver markets reported declines, and the Shanghai exchange rate rebounded, leading to a surge above 720 taels. By Friday, it had reached 730 taels and 2 mace, with a cumulative increase of more than 40 taels. Finally, it slightly weakened, falling sharply by 10 taels, and ended at 719 taels and 2 mace. Considering the high and low points of these five days, there was a difference of 42 taels and 7 mace. Compared to the previous Saturday (the first day of trading in July), it still rose by 4 taels and 2 mace. However, the fluctuations were confusing, and people were flustered, with prices fluctuating constantly. The British and American silver markets contracted again, but the exchange rate had rebounded by 1.75 to 1.875 points. With this, the forward exchange rate became even tighter, with both official and unofficial rates contracting by one notch. The US dollar also slightly contracted by 0.25. Gold industry players and speculators had already sold off. The US dollar occasionally had returned notes. From the beginning of the week, it opened at 42-43 taels, and later only counted 38-39 taels. However, the Chinese merchants roughly sold short 5-6 million yuan, calculated at a listed price of over 70 taels. As for the thin inventory of physical goods, it was necessary to add 11 taels to the spot price. However, there may still be twists and turns in the future, making it difficult to predict. The general situation of the week is summarized below.

(3) The North China area has long been occupied by Japanese yarn, and there is very little hope for Chinese yarn. With all these unfavorable situations, the yarn market is still in a sad state. Fortunately, the inventory of various factories is thinner than before, so the current attitude of manufacturers is very stable. Postal Workers' General Strike 165

— Buddha

The Shanghai postal workers' "Save the Post Office" movement, which had been brewing for a long time, suddenly announced a general strike again yesterday morning.

Because the association proposed a plan to consolidate the postal base, but the Ministry had no sincere intention of accepting it, a general strike was declared starting on the morning of the 22nd. The four conditions put forward by the association are also justifiable and legitimate demands.

Because the government is economically exhausted (why it is exhausted, let's not discuss for the moment), it may be possible to adjust surpluses to offset deficits, and use long to compensate for short. However, the government's use of funds has never been made public, and the people have no right to question it. Ordinary people only see certain dignitaries spending hundreds of thousands to buy foreign houses as residences, and certain dignitaries spending millions to buy villas. The country supports countless useless dignitaries and politicians. Apart from these, there are no benefits to the country or the people to be seen.

The people can only envy, only sigh, only provide their hard-earned money one by one. Please, dignitaries, put yourself in our place and think, isn't this unfair?

Literature and Art 166

On the Songhu Road 167

— Chen Baoren

The oppressive weather marks the early summer days, a weary gaze opens towards Wusong,

The turmoil on the borderlands has yet to cease, unbearable to spur the horse to return once more.

In the waning spring of the fourth month, orioles sadly cry,

A scene of devastation fills the eyes, brimming with tears.

Settle peacefully in your old homes and till your lands,

Cook rice from the water caltrop to nourish the spring plowing.

Heaven and sea shed tears, mourning the loyal souls,

Elders sob, leaning on doorways, sighing.

Ruins of broken walls remain scattered about,

The fragmented remains are too terrible to speak of.

Along the long embankment, willow branches droop as spring ends,

Joyful celebrations unfurl anew beneath the bright sun's flag.

Restore our rivers and mountains, revive our culture and artifacts,

Bestow abundant rain to comfort the common people.

Scientific Luminescent Materials 168

— Lisheng

Materials that continue to emit light in a dark room after exposure to light are mostly alkaline earth metal sulfides. If appropriate compounds are added to these sulfides, luminescent materials of various colors such as red, green, purple, and blue can be produced. The hands and numerals on some watches that can be seen even in the dark are an example of the industrial application of luminescent materials. There are various methods for making them. A few simple ones are introduced below:

(1) Purple Luminescent Material: 20.0 grams of lime or oyster shell ash powder, 6.0 grams of sulfur powder, and 2.0 grams of starch are finely ground and mixed evenly. Then, drip in a solution of 0.5 grams of bismuth nitrate Bi(NO3)5 dissolved in 100 ml of alcohol and a small amount of hydrochloric acid. Place in a fire-resistant container and heat until red-hot for 20 minutes. After cooling, grind into a fine powder and heat again for 15 minutes, but be careful not to overheat and cause it to melt.

(2) Dark Blue Luminescent Material: 20.0 grams of lime, 20.0 grams of barium hydroxide Ba(OH)2, 6.0 grams of sulfur, 1.0 gram each of potassium sulfate K2SO4 and sodium sulfate Na2SO4, 2.0 grams of lithium carbonate Li2Co3, and 2 ml of bismuth nitrate solution (concentration as in the first method), and 2 ml of rubidium nitrate RbNo3 solution (concentration is a ratio of one to one hundred parts water). After mixing well, heat as in the previous method to produce the material.

(3) White Luminescent Material: 0.4 grams of bismuth nitrate, 2.5 grams of table salt, 62.0 grams of sulfur flowers, 65.0 grams of strontium carbonate SrCo3, and 4.0 grams of crystalline sodium carbonate Na2Co3roH2O are mixed and placed in a fire-resistant container, covered with a layer of starch. Heat until red-hot for five minutes, then remove. The white luminescent material is then ready.

(4) Pale Red Luminescent Material: 100.0 grams of oyster shell ash and 25 grams of calcined sea salt powder are mixed with 60.0 to 100.0 grams of sulfur flowers. Place in a fire-resistant container and heat until red-hot. Then add 20.0 grams of strontium sulfide SrS and heat again. After cooling, a pale red luminescent powder is obtained. If strontium sulfide is replaced with barium sulfide BaS, a green luminescent material is obtained. Note: This material should be stored in a glass bottle in a dark place.

(5) Watch Face Luminescent Material: Take zinc sulfide precipitate ZnS and place it in a fire-resistant container, sealing the opening. Heat to white-hot, then add a small amount of copper, lead, or silver (any will do), and mix evenly. Take mesothorium bromide equal to one-thousandth of the weight of the zinc sulfide, dissolve it in water, and drip this solution into the fire-resistant container containing the zinc sulfide, which has been cooled to below 100 degrees. Place the container in a hot water bath and heat until dry. Grind the powder, mix with Canada balsam and a small amount of xylene, and it is ready for use.

(6) By adding thallsnitraf solution to 6.0 grams of sulfur, 40.0 grams of strontium carbonate, 1.0 gram of lithium carbonate, and 1.0 gram of arsenic sulfide As2S3, a light green color can be produced. Other colors such as yellow and ocher can also be produced, but due to length limitations, they are omitted.

A Corner of Society

Aristocratic Doctors 169

— Hongshui

Wu Ma had a boil on her breast, and she had no choice but to find every possible way to get medical treatment.

In a corner of the ×× ward, she sat on the sofa, holding her chest with both hands from time to time, crying out in pain, waiting for the doctor to hurry up and examine her. A young doctor in a Western suit was carefully treating a modern girl. From this soft and gentle breeze, a fragrant scent drifted, mixed with her moans of discomfort.

"Dr. ×, please be kind!" Wu Ma said, almost crying from the pain.

But he only glanced at her, and in the corner of his eye, he showed a look of disgust for Wu Ma, who was wearing a blue jacket and black pants, and was both yellow and thin.

"Hey! Dr. ×… It hurts so much!" Wu Ma seemed to want to get angry, seeing that he was always chatting with that lady about things that had nothing to do with the illness.

"Don't be noisy, don't be noisy! When did it start?" he asked coldly.

"Five days!"

"How are your bowel movements and urination? Any fever?"

"...Yes..."

"Hmm! It's because of internal heat!" he said, shaking his head twice.

"Oh dear! Is it dangerous?" she asked anxiously, frowning tightly.

"What's called dangerous? If you say it's dangerous, it's not dangerous, but if you say it's not dangerous, it might be dangerous!"

"What should I do? Dr. ×!"

"It will cost nine dollars…"

"Okay… okay… Can you make it stronger?"

"Haha, just prescribing this ××× medicine will cost at least five dollars."

"…" Only Wu Ma's eyes narrowed, and a few tears fell. He still thought she was just in too much pain, so he turned to an old lady with a round face, smiling and starting his diagnosis.

Sexual Issues

When Off Work 170

— Yingdai

Human life is unequal, but the inequality caused by humans is even more severe than natural inequality. Needless to say, the leisurely lives of the madams and young ladies in mansions; when the dance hostesses finish their night of selling smiles, in the faint light of dawn, sleepy-eyed, when they return home, it is exactly the time when the female workers in the silk factory, with their lunch boxes, go to work in the silk factory. And there is an absolute difference between the lives of female workers and dance hostesses. In the eyes of ordinary female workers, the life of a dance hostess seems like a goddess descending to earth.

Because behind our school, there are three or four silk factories, so I have quite a bit of insight into the lives of the female workers. When the east turns the color of fish belly, while we are fast asleep, the noisy sounds from the back break our good night's sleep every day. They start working at six o'clock. Those who live far away have to get up at three or four o'clock to cook.

After they enter the silk factory, they don't get off work until six o'clock in the afternoon. Except for a little bit of lunch time, they have to work eleven hours a day, gathering wealth for the factory owners like cattle and horses. Their lives are, of course, extremely hard, but in their own eyes, they don't feel any pain. They pass the days happily, because when they are working, the factory staff often tease and joke with them, and their mouths are also very practiced. They can answer men fluently with both romantic and obscene words. In their eyes, this may be comfort found in hardship!

The liveliest time is of course when they get off work. In the morning, when they go to work, they enter the factory in scattered groups, but when they get off work, they come out together. At that time, because of the day's labor, they are happy to go home to rest, and their faces are filled with smiles. They excitedly carry their lunch baskets out. This forms a perfect inverse proportion to the listless and dispirited attitude when they go to work. "Zhao Di!" "Lin Di!" "Gen Di!" "Zhao Di's mother!" "Lin Di's older sister!" A lively sound fills the air of the streets.

The idle, good-for-nothing, and frivolous young men, from experience, already know the time when the silk factory gets off work. Before six o'clock, they will gather at the entrance of the silk factory as if by agreement, waiting for these female workers to come out. The older women, of course, can be safe and sound, but the younger, more fashionable female workers, when they come out three together or two in a group, are inevitably surrounded and teased at will. Some of them run away like small birds seeing hungry eagles, while others curse and laugh, calling them "rotten corpses" and "rascals." But when they are cursed, they not only don't get angry, but instead show smiles, as if hoping that they will curse a few more times, thinking that they have achieved a considerable victory.

Among them, there are also some who ride bicycles, intentionally going very slowly, to block their way. Wherever they go, the bicycles follow. These things, except on days when work is stopped, are found around our school every day.

A Street Test of Business Acumen, Part One 171

The Time Spent Gazing at Store Windows

Recently, competition among stores has become increasingly fierce. As a result, merchants have made amazing progress in the study of window displays. In prosperous cities and busy streets, we feel that the items displayed in the store windows on both sides are constantly changing with competitive designs, novel patterns, and unique arrangements. This is because modern merchants are well aware that if they do not study window displays carefully, they will not be able to attract passersby to stop and watch, and their business may fail as a result. Therefore, they must pay attention to window display.

The progress of window display has indeed achieved great results. You see, outside every store, there are always many passersby stopping to watch the items in the window. So, what is the average time each person spends watching the window? This is certainly an interesting question. It is said that the average time a man spends watching outside the window is three-tenths of a second less than a woman.

The results of this test were obtained over two years, after surveying 9,071 people. As a result, we know that the average time each passerby spends gazing at the window is 18.7 seconds. Women spend an average of 17.6 seconds watching outside the window, but if they are walking with another woman, the time spent watching the window increases to 20 seconds. If a man is walking with a woman, they spend an average of 20.9 seconds watching outside the window. Therefore, from these 9,071 people, we can obtain the following statistics:

A woman walking alone: 17.6 seconds

A man walking alone: 17.3 seconds

Two women: 20.0 seconds

A man and a woman: 20.9 seconds

Undoubtedly, women's time is mostly spent gazing at the windows of jewelry stores, while men mostly gaze at the windows of bookstores. In these places, they spend an average of 29 seconds, which is the longest viewing time.

Family Life

Economy and Family 172

— Zeyong

One afternoon, the weather was very hot and stuffy, so I went to a certain park to relax by myself.

In the deep shade of a corner, a modern young couple sat on a public bench, leaning close to each other, talking about their love. I couldn't help but be curious, so I secretly hid behind a tree to eavesdrop on their whispered secrets. The woman asked first, "Dear Mr. He, why are you so unhappy today?"

"Because yesterday my father told me that he had arranged a marriage for me with another woman, and the wedding will be held next month!" This was the man's reply. "Well, then you should marry that woman!" the woman said, with what seemed like a touch of jealousy in her tone.

"Ah! Dear Ms. Feng! Please don't doubt me. Besides you in my mind, no matter what, I will not marry another woman, because you are the angel in my heart!" the young man said to comfort her.

"Since that's the case, then you should break away from your family!"

"No… no, I dare not break away from my family…" the young man paused, and then said pantingly.

"Why can't you break away?"

"If I break away from my family, I will cut off my source of income!"

When I heard this, I couldn't help but sigh three times, so I went home to record it and submit it to this publication for the study of love among young men and women in general.

When I saw this manuscript, I discovered a common fallacy in the minds of young people these days. Modern marriage is based on freedom as a principle, which is true enough. If a young person already has an angel in their heart, but their parents insist on forcing them to marry another woman, this is indeed the parents' fault. In this day and age, parents should no longer overstep their bounds and make decisions for their children. However, young people must know that a happy family must have a good economy to maintain it. If you only talk about freedom of marriage, and do not first solve the problem of economic independence, this is a big mistake. If the family is originally wealthy, there may be no problem, but if the family is not wealthy, then young people should first seek the ability and methods of making a living. Freedom should be thorough, and not just partial. The current big family system has fundamentally shaken, and it should be economically independent to organize small families. The current family system in Europe and America is originally like this.

Art's Tail 173

Waste of Life 174

— Wuwei

(One of my miscellaneous feelings)

"Do you want ingots…?"

Under the dim light, such a voice came from the alley, reminding me that today is the fifteenth day of the lunar calendar.

From this desolate cry, I am reminded of the difficulty in changing customs. Old ideas still shroud the minds of a portion of the people, and the pitifulness of these producers. In our Zhejiang, in Shaoxing prefecture alone, there are more than 500,000 people engaged in the manufacture of tin foil! (the raw material for ingots!) Combining the whole province, there are no less than one million people. The capital used is no less than tens of millions of yuan. In this way, from the hands of the tin foil workers, it is transferred to the hands of the old women who make the ingots to sell to consumers, and then the ash from the foil is bought back and reprocessed. A meaningless cycle of production controls the fate of more than a million people. If we examine the value of their production, it consumes the material resources of the real human world! (food, clothing, housing, transportation, etc.!) What does it contribute to the unknowable underworld? This is an extremely comical phenomenon in our country's production sector. As a result, Zhejiang Province is equivalent to being short of one million people, and the country's 474 million people lose the productivity of one million people. The productivity of these one million people is all lost to the land of nothingness. I can't name it, so I call it "waste of life."

Source

The Second and Sixteenth Days 175

— Shengwu

"Sir, boss, do a good deed, save the poor, cultivate virtue for your children and grandchildren." Every second or sixteenth day of the lunar calendar, from morning to dusk, there are always many beggars, men, women, old and young, who come to visit and plead in this way.

"Give him a copper coin and tell him not to come next time," a gentleman-like person said to his apprentice. "To prevent him from coming next time, we shouldn't give him anything this time, otherwise wouldn't it be inviting a wolf into the house?" As a result of the conversation, the beggar, of course, suffered a loss.

At first, on these days (the second or sixteenth), some gave and some didn't. As a result of the distribution, it never reached one hundred copper coins. Recently, it seems to be more than before. I wanted to know how much it would be in a day, so yesterday (April 16th) I distributed as much as possible. Later, I calculated that a total of 173 copper coins were given out, breaking the previous record. Beggars are gradually increasing, and public security will certainly be in danger. I wonder if those who are responsible for local public security are also considering this.
